## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (classical mechanics: nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly time t, which is the standard state-space form of a (non)linear second-order oscillator. Typical models combine restoring forces (functions of x), dissipation (functions of v), and external/parametric forcing (functions of t and/or x).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (undamped): dv_dt = c0 * x (Hooke-type restoring acceleration, sign absorbed into c0)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring plus linear viscous damping via c1)
- Driven damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (external periodic forcing)
- Constant + linear stiffness bias: dv_dt = c0 + c1 * x + c2 * v (gravity/offset plus linear stiffness and damping)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Quadratic + cubic stiffness mix: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (asymmetric nonlinearity and higher-order stiffness)
- Pendulum (sine restoring): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (large-angle pendulum-like restoring with damping)
- Nonlinear drag (quadratic): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-type damping combined with restoring force)
- Mixed linear + cubic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (amplitude-dependent dissipation)
- Van der Pol form (negative linear damping, positive nonlinear damping): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (self-excited oscillations / limit cycle)
- Rayleigh damping form (velocity-dependent self-excitation): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - v**2) * v (another canonical self-oscillator structure)
- Mathieu/parametric excitation: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (time-varying stiffness leading to parametric resonance)
- Nonlinear frequency modulation: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) + c4 * v (Duffing with external drive and damping)
- Conservative potential force form: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) + c3 * v (polynomial potential gradient plus damping; minus sign can be absorbed into coefficients)
- Rational softening/hardening stiffness: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x / (c2 + x**2) + c3 * v (effective stiffness that changes with amplitude without blow-up)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope тЖТ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects тЖТ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay тЖТ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior тЖТ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects тЖТ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative oscillators often have dv_dt dominated by an odd restoring term in x (e.g., x, x**3, sin(c*x)), implying symmetry under (x,v)->(-x,-v) when forcing is absent.
- Linear viscous damping appears as a term proportional to v; amplitude-dependent damping is often captured by v*Abs(v) or v**3 and changes decay rate with speed.
- External periodic forcing typically enters additively as sin(c*t+c) or cos(c*t+c), producing sustained oscillations and resonance when the forcing frequency matches the natural frequency.
- Parametric excitation is suggested when x is multiplied by a periodic function of t (e.g., (c0+c1*cos(c*t))*x), leading to Mathieu-type instability tongues.
- Self-excited (limit-cycle) behavior is commonly modeled by a damping coefficient that changes sign with amplitude, e.g., (c - x**2)*v or (c - v**2)*v.
- Hardening/softening springs are indicated by cubic stiffness terms in x**3: positive cubic increases oscillation frequency with amplitude (hardening), negative decreases it (softening).
- Asymmetric oscillators (non-centrosymmetric restoring force) often require even powers of x (x**2, x**4) or a constant offset term in dv_dt.
- If energy is approximately conserved (weak damping/forcing), dv_dt is mostly a function of x alone (dv_dt тЙИ f(x)), with v-terms small corrections.
- Piecewise or non-smooth phenomena (impacts, dry friction) are often approximated by terms involving Abs(v) or sign-like behavior; smooth surrogates include v*Abs(v).
- Nonlinear frequency shifts with amplitude are frequently captured by adding higher-order odd terms in x (x**3, x**5) rather than introducing explicit t-dependence.

### Core blocking reason (applies to all candidates with logs)
GT requires \(\log(|v|+1)\). Every candidate log is of the form \(\log(c\cdot v+1)\) with **no absolute value**. Since \(v\) takes negative values, there is no real constant \(c\) such that \(c v + 1 \equiv |v|+1\) for all \(v\). Therefore none of those candidates can be globally equivalent to GT.

Additionally, GT needs an \(x|v|^{1/3}\) term; candidates only offer \(x v^{p}\) (no abs) or other \(x\)-structures.

Therefore no candidate can be made identical to GT by parameter choice.

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT numerical expression:**
`-0.0441723*v┬│ - 0.333481*v*(1 - v┬▓) - 1.24947*v - 3.58221*x*(0.047928*|v|^(1/3) + 1) - 0.624737*log(|v| + 1)`

Let me expand this:
- `-0.0441723*v┬│`
- `-0.333481*v + 0.333481*v┬│`
- `-1.24947*v`
- `-3.58221*x - 3.58221*0.047928*|v|^(1/3)*x`
- `-0.624737*log(|v| + 1)`

Combining terms:
- **v┬│**: (-0.0441723 + 0.333481) = 0.289309*v┬│
- **v**: (-0.333481 - 1.24947) = -1.58295*v
- **x**: -3.58221*x
- **|v|^(1/3)*x**: -0.17166*x*|v|^(1/3)
- **log(|v|+1)**: -0.624737*log(|v| + 1)

So GT = c_a*x + c_b*v + c_c*v┬│ + c_d*log(|v|+1) + c_e*|v|^(1/3)*x

**Key basis functions in GT:**
1. `x` (linear)
2. `v` (linear)
3. `v┬│`
4. `log(|v| + 1)` тАФ note this uses `|v|`, not `v`
5. `|v|^(1/3) * x` тАФ this is `v^(1/3)*x` only for v>0

**Important:** The GT has `log(Abs(v) + 1)` and `Abs(v)^(1/3)*x`. Since v takes both signs, `log(c*v + 1)` is NOT the same as `log(|v| + 1)`.

Also, `v^c6*x` where c6=1/3: for negative v, `v^(1/3)` is real (cube root) but `|v|^(1/3)` differs in sign. So `v^(1/3)*x тЙа |v|^(1/3)*x` for negative v.

Let me check which candidates have the right structure. The GT needs:
- No `v┬▓` term (or it can be zeroed)
- No `t` dependence
- `log(|v| + 1)` тАФ candidates with `log(c*v + 1)` fail since v can be negative
- `|v|^(1/3)*x` тАФ candidates with `v^c*x` fail since `v^(1/3) тЙа |v|^(1/3)` for negative v

**Critical issue with log:** `log(|v| + 1)` vs `log(c*v + 1)`: These are fundamentally different for negative v. No constant choice makes them equal.

**Critical issue with |v|^(1/3)*x:** `|v|^(1/3)` vs `v^(1/3)`: For negative v, `v^(1/3) = -|v|^(1/3)`, so these differ. No candidate using `v^c6*x` can match `|v|^(1/3)*x`.

Wait тАФ but the GT also has no standalone `|v|` term. Many candidates have `c*Abs(v)`. Since GT doesn't need it, we can set that coefficient to 0.

Given the two critical issues (log and |v|^(1/3)), **no candidate can exactly match the GT** because:
1. All candidates with `log` use `log(c*v + 1)`, not `log(|v| + 1)`
2. All candidates use `v^c*x`, not `|v|^c*x`

Since v takes both positive and negative values, these are genuinely different functions.

After careful analysis of all 50 candidates, none can match the GT exactly.
